Summary of Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) Trend Analysis

This analysis was conducted based on the latest technical data to identify the core trends and key application areas of AI transformation (AX) in the manufacturing industry. As a result of the analysis, AI is establishing itself as a core driver that innovates productivity and quality, going beyond simple automation.

The most notable areas are automation of defect detection through 'AI visual inspection' and 'Root Cause Analysis (RCA) using 'Causal Inference AI'. These technologies directly contribute to yield improvement and quality stabilization and have received high evaluations. Additionally, predictive maintenance, process optimization, and production planning and scheduling optimization are key application areas commonly emphasized in various resources, enabling data-driven efficient factory operation.

Key trends include the start of discussions on the introduction of 'Agentic AI' that solves problems autonomously, going beyond traditional predictive analytics, and 'humanoid robots'. This suggests that the role of AI is expanding beyond the production floor to encompass the entire value chain, including supply chain management and work redesign.

While opportunities lie in clear productivity improvement and quality enhancement, in areas requiring high reliability, such as GAMP 5 cases in the pharmaceutical industry, AI system validation and regulatory compliance remain important challenges. For a successful AI transformation, it is necessary to start in areas where clear ROI can be expected, such as visual inspection, and gradually prepare a strategy for the phased introduction of advanced technologies like causal inference and agentic AI.

Integrating neural-symbolic causal inference into manufacturing copilot workflows, connecting predictionâ€“explanationâ€“intervention, it leverages LiNGAM+DiffAN along with bootstrap edge stability and total causal effects to refine Root Cause Analysis (RCA) prioritization and predictive maintenance/process decision-making. It supports semantically validated graph modifications via knowledge graph and ontology-based Operator-in-the-loop, continuously improves the model through counterfactual validation, and ensures real-world applicability through staged deployment from TaaS to OPC UA/MQTT.

This article specifically presents a method to implement predictionâ€“explanationâ€“intervention within a single system by integrating a causal inference-based CausalTrace agent into a manufacturing copilot (SmartPilot). Highly reliable DAGs are created using LiNGAM/DiffAN and bootstrap stability scores, and causal hypotheses are data-drivenly confirmed through total causal effects and counterfactual verification. Through knowledge graphs and ontologies, the meaning of units, process constraints, and sensor data is transparently provided to operators, and field applicability is enhanced with interactive graph modification and evidence tracing functions. In an actual rocket assembly testbed, RCA performance (e.g., MAP@3 94%) and explanation quality (ROUGE-1 0.91) were demonstrated, and we cover the virtual-to-real environment deployment procedure from TaaS to OPC UA/MQTT, as well as future distributed/edge transition strategies. Through this approach, manufacturing sites can implement high-reliability root cause analysis, strengthened human-AI collaboration, and phased deployment and performance indicator-based operations.

For robot adoption, switch to a simulation-first approach, utilizing NVIDIA Isaac Sim-based digital twins, domain randomization, and virtual-to-real data loops to reduce development lead time and cost, and increase real-world transfer success rates. For unstructured and highly variable processes, begin with humanoid/collaborative cells as small-scale pilots, gradually expanding from standardizeable tasks (e.g., BMW and Mercedes cases). For logistics and lineside applications, apply AI autonomy stacks, including multi-agent path planning and dynamic allocation, to enhance throughput and responsiveness. During this process, visualize ROI by ensuring compliance with OPC UA and safety standards, and through KPI management of cycle time, utilization rate, and the sim-to-real performance gap, utilizing Xiaomi and Tesla cases as benchmarks.

In the strictly regulated environment of pharmaceutical manufacturing, proven AI application methods can be immediately extended to general manufacturing: while focusing on immediate value areas (predictive maintenance, real-time quality control RTRT, process optimization), first establish a CPPÂ·PPVâ€“CQA connection map by standardizing MES/LIMS/Historian/batch records, and secure explainability and regulatory acceptance with a mechanistic+ML hybrid approach. This article presents a strategic framework for systematically applying AI to planning, supply chain, demand, and real-time response to address external variabilities such as strikes, weather, and port congestion. The key learning points are 1) demand sensing that integrates even external unstructured signals, 2) scenario planning through constraint-based scheduling and digital twins, 3) real-time event detection and response playbook execution as a control tower, and 4) transition from S&OP to IBP and establishment of DataOps/MLOps-based operational governance. Managing performance with specific metrics (OTIF, inventory turnover, schedule adherence, etc.) and an approach that controls model risk with Human-in-the-loop are effective for practical application.

According to a Deloitte report, agent-type AI should be designed as collaborative agents that augment human decision-making across all areas of product development, production, quality, and supply chain, rather than replacing the workforce. It is realistic to begin with a copilot phase that incorporates Human-in-the-Loop (HITL) approval, transparent communication, and upskilling. Assuming scalability, securely integrate with MES/ERP/PLM and SCM, and internalize security and governance, including role-based access, audit logs, and sandbox/approval workflows, to ensure reliability. As priority initiatives, identify NPI change management, production planning and scheduling, quality issue triage/8D, equipment maintenance ticket automation, and supplier communication, and quantify the effects using KPIs such as cycle time, lead time, First-Time-Right/scrap rate, downtime/MTTR, and compliance events, while simultaneously redesigning SOP/RACI.

Deloitte suggests that Agent AI will accelerate manufacturing innovation as autonomous copilots assisting humans throughout the entire process of design, production, quality, and distribution. The key is (1) system integration and security/governance predicated on scale, (2) job redesign and transparent change management, and (3) phased expansion after reliability verification through pilots. Initially, managing risks based on Human-in-the-Loop (HITL), an approach that starts with high-value workflows such as New Product Introduction (NPI), production planning, and quality triage, and then verifies effectiveness using KPIs like cycle time, First-Time-Right, and downtime, is practical.

This review systematically organizes AI/ML applications across the entire lifecycle of pharmaceutical manufacturing (predictive maintenance, real-time quality inspection, process optimization, supply chain & inventory optimization, regulatory compliance automation) and presents some quantitative effects (e.g., 30% reduction in downtime). GAMP 4ì—ì„œ GAMP 5ë¡œ ì „í™˜í•˜ë©´ ìœ„í—˜ê¸°ë°˜ ìˆ˜ëª…ì£¼ê¸°ì™€ ì‹œìŠ¤í…œ ë“±ê¸‰ë³„ ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¼ë§ì„ í†µí•´ ê²€ì¦ ë²”ìœ„ë¥¼ ìµœì í™”í•˜ê³ , ë²¤ë” ë¬¸ì„œì™€ í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ/IaC ê¸°ë°˜ ì¸í”„ë¼ ìê²©ì„ ì ê·¹ ìˆ˜ìš©í•˜ì—¬ ë¬¸ì„œ ì¤‘ë³µê³¼ ìˆ˜ì‘ì—…ì„ ì¤„ì´ë©´ì„œ(í”„ë¡œë¹„ì €ë‹ 50% ë‹¨ì¶•, ìˆ˜ì‘ì—… 70% ê°ì†Œ) ê·œì œ ì í•©ì„±ê³¼ ë°ì´í„° ë¬´ê²°ì„±ì„ ê°•í™”í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ëŠ” í¬ë¦¬í‹°ì»¬ ì”½í‚¹ ì¤‘ì‹¬ìœ¼ë¡œ ì¬êµ¬ì„±í•˜ê³ , AI/MLì€ ìš”êµ¬ì‚¬í•­Â·ë°ì´í„°/ëª¨ë¸ í˜•ìƒê´€ë¦¬Â·ë“œë¦¬í”„íŠ¸ í†µì œ ë° ê°ì‚¬ì¶”ì /ì ‘ê·¼í†µì œ ë“± ë¬´ê²°ì„± ì„¤ê³„ë¥¼ í†µí•´ GxP ë‚´ ê²€ì¦ì´ ê°€ëŠ¥í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì‹¤í–‰ì€ QRM(ICH Q9) ë‚´ì¬í™”, ìœ„í—˜ê¸°ë°˜ SOP/í…œí”Œë¦¿, ê³µê¸‰ì—…ì²´ í‰ê°€Â·ì¦ê±° ì—°ê³„, ì¶”ì ì„± ë§¤íŠ¸ë¦­ìŠ¤Â·í˜•ìƒê´€ë¦¬ ë„êµ¬ ë„ì…, ìš´ì˜/ë³€ê²½/íê¸°ê¹Œì§€ QMS í†µí•©ìœ¼ë¡œ ì¶”ì§„í•˜ì‹­ì‹œì˜¤. Transitioning from GAMP 4 to GAMP 5 allows for optimizing validation scope through a risk-based lifecycle and system category-based scaling, and strengthening regulatory compliance and data integrity by actively adopting vendor documentation and cloud/IaC-based infrastructure qualification, thereby reducing document duplication and manual work (50% reduction in provisioning, 70% decrease in manual work). Testing should be reconfigured around critical thinking, and AI/ML can be validated within GxP through integrity design including requirements, data/model configuration management, drift control, and audit trail/access control. Execution should be driven by QMS integration up to operation/change/decommissioning, including internalization of QRM (ICH Q9), risk-based SOPs/templates, supplier evaluation and evidence linkage, and introduction of traceability matrices and configuration management tools.

CAPEXÂ·ì±„ìš© ê³„íšì— ê´€ì„¸Â·ì´ë¯¼ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ ë¯¼ê°ë„ ë¶„ì„ì„ í¬í•¨í•˜ê³ , ë‹¨ê¸° ì¸ë ¥ë‚œ í•´ì†Œí˜• ìë™í™”ì™€ ì¤‘ì¥ê¸° ìŠ¤ë§ˆíŠ¸íŒ©í† ë¦¬ ë¡œë“œë§µì„ êµ¬ë¶„í•´ íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿â†’í™•ì‚° ì²´í¬ë¦¬ìŠ¤íŠ¸ë¡œ ìš´ì˜í•˜ë©°, ì¬ë°°ì¹˜ìœ¨Â·êµìœ¡ì´ìˆ˜ìœ¨ ë“± ì‚¬ëŒ ì¤‘ì‹¬ KPIë¥¼ ëª¨ë‹ˆí„°ë§í•˜ë¼. Manufacturing job decline is not solely an AI/automation problem but a result of intertwined factors like labor supply (aging population, immigration), policies such as tariffs, and investment timing. AI can be a means to simultaneously alleviate labor shortages and enhance productivity. The automation transition should be designed as a redeployment strategy rather than a replacement strategy. Key elements include redesigning roles such as cobot operators and AI quality supervisors, internalizing talent pipelines through reskilling/micro-credentials and partnerships with local educational institutions, and on-site execution encompassing change management, safety, and ergonomics. Include tariff and immigration risk sensitivity analysis in CAPEX and hiring plans. Differentiate between short-term labor shortage-alleviating automation and long-term smart factory roadmaps, operating them with a pilot-to-scale checklist. Monitor human-centric KPIs such as redeployment rates and training completion rates.

In the 'second robotics revolution' triggered by generative AI, China's concentration on robots and components and the weakening industrial depth in the West increase supply chain and TCO risks, so manufacturers must internalize AI-robot integration capabilities as a core competency. In terms of talent, acquire capabilities in robot programming, digital twin, perception/path planning, and ISO 10218/13849, and quantify the effects with KPIs (OEE, MTBF, lead time, quality) to adjust investment priorities.

The core insight of the article is that to achieve 'AI-robot innovation,' software capabilities alone are insufficient, and industrial depth encompassing robot manufacturing, parts, system integration, and verification is necessary. Manufacturers should, premising the risk of a China-centric robot supply chain, design dual-sourcing and localization strategies, and while utilizing open-source and open-stack to increase development speed and flexibility, concurrently implement safety and security governance. A*STAR's industry-academia collaboration cases (Mencast Marine, Abrasive Engineering) demonstrate process optimization and cost reduction through intelligent and adaptive factory solutions like AIMie, showing that the risk of AI adoption for SMEs and mid-sized manufacturers can be lowered. The Sigma case, which involved incrementally layering ML on SAP IBP to initially improve forecast accuracy by 5-10% and then further by approximately 10%, directly impacts the tangible ROI (inventory turnover, service level, prevention of lost sales) in manufacturing demand and supply planning. For implementation, manage the share of 'innovation revenue' by mapping your portfolio to the AI value chain, and concretize this through an Edge AI sensor pilot â†’ line â†’ full factory rollout, customized high-density cooling and power solutions for data center customers, and EMS upgrades.

This report demonstrates with data that AI is driving greater growth across the entire value chain (semiconductors â€“ cloud â€“ networking â€“ power â€“ cooling â€“ sensors) than 'software end-apps'. Areas directly related to manufacturing (industrial automation, edge AI sensing/predictive maintenance, robotics, HVAC/thermal management, power infrastructure) are growing rapidly, and companies with innovative technologies are achieving outsized growth compared to commoditized players (e.g., Trane vs. Equinix, Siemens). Manufacturers should map their portfolios to the AI value chain, introduce 'innovation revenue share' as a KPI, prioritize investments in edge AI sensing and energy/power infrastructure upgrades, and align their product roadmaps and supply chain strategies with data center demand (power, cooling) and hyperscaler CAPEX.

This report presents immediately applicable operational strategies from the perspective of manufacturing AI Transformation (AX), with precision fermentation, green ammonia, and AI-based waste upcycling as key pillars, encompassing bioreactor operation (PAT, digital twin, predictive control), P2A-based energy and production schedule optimization (EMS, storage linkage), and automatic sorting by computer vision, hyperspectral (imaging), and robotics. In the pilot and scale-up phases, through modular skids/CMO, IIoT safety sensing and HAZOP, and a KPI system (OEE, purity rate, conversion yield, landfill avoidance, carbon), cost, quality, and carbon can be simultaneously improved, and the reduction of Scope 1, 2, and 3 emissions and the transition to a circular economy can be accelerated.

The WEF report shows that the low-carbon and circular transition of manufacturing processes can be accelerated through precision fermentation, green ammonia, and AI-based waste upcycling. Food, materials, and chemical manufacturers can reduce energy and raw material costs and simultaneously reduce Scope 1, 2, and 3 emissions by combining investments in bioreactors, electrolyzers, and robotics with process digitalization (PAT, digital twin, predictive control). Practically, the following are recommended: 1) discovery of high-value by-products and AI-based sorting pilots, 2) renewable energy-linked P2A production scheduling, 3) pre-validation of precision fermentation raw materials, quality, and regulations (labeling), 4) EPC retrofit and establishment of safety (IIoT, HAZOP) systems, and 5) phased rollout based on KPIs (purity rate, methane avoidance, conversion yield, carbon/cost reduction).

ASML's Q3 2025 results indicate that the proliferation of EUV and High-NA, along with the introduction of advanced packaging equipment (new XT:260), is rapidly increasing the difficulty and throughput demands of lithography and packaging processes, and that equipment-embedded AI (Mistral collaboration) shortens yield and ramp-up through recipe optimization, automatic calibration, and predictive maintenance. Accordingly, semiconductor manufacturers need to prioritize building lithography/packaging OEE rebalancing, MES-track-inspection data integration, real-time SPC and defect detection AI, data governance, and MLOps, while simultaneously monetizing installed base services and addressing China regulatory risks (dual sourcing, capacity scenarios).

ASML's Q3 2025 results confirm the trend of increasing lithography intensity due to the expansion of EUV adoption and AI demand (leading-edge logic and HBM DRAM). The up to 4x productivity of the i-line XT:260 for advanced packaging will trigger a redesign of packaging line bottlenecks, and through cooperation with Mistral AI, the application of embedded AI to enhance equipment performance and yield is expected to accelerate. From a manufacturing AX perspective, digital twin-based bottleneck analysis, strengthening equipment-data pipelines, MLOps systems for recipe optimization and predictive maintenance, and the establishment of scenarios to address regulatory risks (especially the slowdown in China sales) are presented as practical implementation challenges.

The edge-cloud data fabric example, where the entire NFL stadium was transformed into a data center, provides an execution blueprint for optimizing cost/performance in manufacturing sites. This is achieved by performing low-latency inference on large-volume video/sensor streams for multi-camera quality inspection, safety monitoring, and equipment anomaly diagnosis, and by utilizing object storage tiering and data lifecycle management. Data consistency, ensured through decoupled MLOps for on-site inference and central learning, along with caching, replication, and metadata standardization between on-site and AWS/Azure/GCP, can be immediately applied to hybrid/multi-cloud architectures for multi-factory, multi-region operations.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
NFL-ë„·ì•± ì‚¬ë¡€ëŠ” â€˜ê²½ê¸°ì¥=ë°ì´í„° ì„¼í„°â€™ ê´€ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ëŒ€ìš©ëŸ‰ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ë°ì´í„°ë¥¼ ì—£ì§€ì—ì„œ ì²˜ë¦¬í•˜ê³  í´ë¼ìš°ë“œì™€ ì¼ê´€ì„± ìˆê²Œ ì—°ê³„í•˜ëŠ” êµ¬ì¡°ë¥¼ ì œì‹œí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡°ì—…ì€ ë©€í‹°ì¹´ë©”ë¼ í’ˆì§ˆê²€ì‚¬Â·ì•ˆì „ ëª¨ë‹ˆí„°ë§ ë“±ì—ì„œ ìœ ì‚¬í•œ ë°ì´í„° ê·œëª¨ì™€ ì €ì§€ì—° ìš”êµ¬ë¥¼ ê°–ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë”°ë¼ì„œ ì—£ì§€ ì¸í¼ëŸ°ìŠ¤+ì¤‘ì•™ ì¬í•™ìŠµì˜ MLOps íŒŒì´í”„ë¼ì¸, í‹°ì–´ë§Â·ë³µì œÂ·ë©”íƒ€ë°ì´í„° í‘œì¤€í™”ë¥¼ í¬í•¨í•œ ë°ì´í„° íŒŒë¸Œë¦­, í•˜ì´í¼ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¼ëŸ¬ ì—°ê³„ë¥¼ í†µí•œ í•˜ì´ë¸Œë¦¬ë“œ í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ ìš´ì˜ì„ ì„¤ê³„í•˜ë©´ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì •ê³¼ ìš´ì˜ íƒ„ë ¥ì„±ì„ ë†’ì¼ ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. The NFL-NetApp case presents a structure that processes large-volume real-time data at the edge, viewing the 'stadium as a data center,' and consistently integrates it with the cloud. The manufacturing industry has similar data volumes and low-latency requirements in areas such as multi-camera quality inspection and safety monitoring. Therefore, by designing an MLOps pipeline of edge inference + central retraining, a data fabric including tiering, replication, and metadata standardization, and hybrid cloud operations through hyper-scaler integration, real-time decision-making and operational resilience can be enhanced.

In AI-based manufacturing transformation, data-centric security for unstructured assets such as documents and drawings is key. By consistently applying role-based access, dynamic watermarking, and activity logs to critical files like CAD across VDI/local/external collaboration, and by identifying and prioritizing the protection of Crown Jewels through a secure collaboration platform that allows for permissions, expiration, and tracking, coupled with unstructured data classification, you can simultaneously lower IP leakage and regulatory risks. Furthermore, by controlling generative AI/Copilot uploads and prompt leakage with policies and establishing an audit system, you can quantify and operate security and compliance performance while maintaining supply chain collaboration speed.

Fasoo introduced a data-centric security strategy to protect manufacturing IP at ManuSec USA 2025. The core of the strategy is to combine granular access policies, dynamic watermarking, and activity logs for unstructured data such as CAD drawings within a VDI environment, and to apply secure collaboration with partners that enables rights, expiration, and tracking. Furthermore, an approach is presented that identifies the location of sensitive data through data radar-ing and progressively extends protection starting from priority assets. This can be utilized as a practical security framework to reduce IP leakage and regulatory risks and maintain the pace of innovation, especially in the AI era where design data proliferates across models and supply chains.

This article presents strategies for AI adoption and workforce transition that are immediately applicable in manufacturing sites. The core lies in employee-driven, bottom-up adoption and achieving rapid results in the areas of documentation and decision-making support. Based on this, specific tasks can be derived, such as university-industry joint PoCs (line-level Digital Twin and Predictive Maintenance), Edge AI quality inspection and equipment condition monitoring, establishment of OT security and Explainable AI guidelines, and factory energy optimization projects.

This document is a list of graduate research areas, but it presents meaningful directions from a manufacturing AX perspective. Specifically, it directly links to core smart factory stacks such as Digital Twin, AI/ML-based machining optimization, Predictive Maintenance, AM, Robotics/Control, Edge, Cloud, 5G/6G, OT Security, Optical/Photonics Sensors, and Smart Grid/Power Electronics. In terms of practical application, it can be developed into small-scale pilots (line-level Digital Twin/Predictive Maintenance), Edge AI quality inspection/condition monitoring, Explainable AI-based process decision-making, DfAM/composite material lightweighting, joint research on factory energy optimization, and more. Overall, it is a useful reference for strategic technology scanning and identifying industry-academia collaboration topics.

RPA/BPO ì¤‘ì‹¬ ìë™í™”ì˜ ëŒ€ì²´ ìœ„í—˜ì„ ê°ì•ˆí•´ Microsoft CopilotÂ·Salesforce Einstein ë“± í”Œë«í¼ ìƒíƒœê³„ í™œìš©ê³¼ í•¨ê»˜ FinOps(íƒœê¹…Â·ì‡¼ë°±/ì°¨ì§€ë°±Â·ì˜ˆì•½/ìŠ¤íŒŸÂ·ë°ì´í„° ìˆ˜ëª…ì£¼ê¸°) ë° ì œë¡œíŠ¸ëŸ¬ìŠ¤íŠ¸Â·XDR ë“± ë³´ì•ˆ ë‚´ì¬í™”ë¥¼ ë³‘í–‰í•˜ê³ , í•´ë‹¹ ì—­ëŸ‰ì„ ê°–ì¶˜ íŒŒíŠ¸ë„ˆì™€ì˜ í˜‘ì—…ì„ ìš°ì„ ì‹œí•˜ì„¸ìš”. Q2 2025 technology services M&A is seeing a premium concentrated on AI, data, and cloud capabilities, and manufacturing must integrate OT/IT data into a lakehouse (Databricks/Snowflake) and combine domain LLM and Agentic AI to automatically orchestrate operational decision-making such as predictive maintenance, process optimization, and yield improvement. Considering the risk of replacement for RPA/BPO-centric automation, alongside utilizing platform ecosystems like Microsoft Copilot and Salesforce Einstein, it is necessary to simultaneously internalize FinOps (tagging, showback/chargeback, reserved/spot, data lifecycle) and security like Zero Trust and XDR, and prioritize collaboration with partners possessing these capabilities.

This report shows that IT service and SaaS M&A in Q2 2025 are focusing on AI, data, and cloud, particularly agentic AI and the Databricks/Snowflake ecosystems. Manufacturing companies should quickly internalize vertical-specific AI based on OT/IT integrated data lakehouse, cloud FinOps, and OT/IT cybersecurity systems. As partners with capabilities to leverage platform ecosystems (Copilot, Einstein, Fusion) receive a premium, when selecting vendors or considering acquisitions, it is practical to use recurring revenue, retention rate, profitability, automation capabilities, and industry-specific experience as key indicators. For geopolitical and tariff risks, a strategy of responding with phased investments (minority, carve-out) and portfolio diversification is effective.

This is a real-world example of an internal combustion engine (ICE) parts manufacturer transitioning to EV, ADAS, and medical sectors, demonstrating the importance of AX governance that connects external intelligence (such as KISTI) with technology roadmaps and investment priorities. Competitiveness can be expanded by establishing a digital thread that connects material-process-performance data, centered around titanium and aluminum-based lightweighting and titanium forming patents, along with process simulation and AI optimization (springback, thermal cycle, mold conditions). For HMLV product groups such as EV brakes, ADAS cases, and medical implants, an operational system is practical that incorporates modular automation, vision inspection, and MES/eDHR traceability, alongside synchronizing dual-source production between Korea and Vietnam across multi-plant OEE, FPY, and cycle time.

Hanguk PIM is diversifying from internal combustion engine (ICE) parts to EV brakes, ADAS camera housings, medical implants, etc., based on KISTI's market and technology analysis, and differentiating itself with lightweight materials such as titanium/aluminum and forming patents. A strategy to diversify costs and risks is evident by operating automated lines in Korea and production bases in Vietnam in parallel. From an AX perspective, the application points include establishing a technology roadmap based on external intelligence, connecting material-process-performance data (digital thread), simulation and AI optimization of titanium forming, modular automation, vision inspection, and traceability tailored for HMLV, and remote monitoring based on multi-plant indicators. Although quantitative data is insufficient, it holds reference value in terms of transition strategy and process/material direction.

With the launch of the 'one team' comprising the Presidential Strategic Committee and three ministries, along with the Manufacturing and Industrial AI Transformation (AX) TF, budgets, regulations, and standards will be consistently advanced, and opportunities for public tenders, subsidies, and pilot projects focused on small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs), mid-sized companies, and regional key industries are expected to expand. It is advantageous for manufacturing companies to proactively establish systems for process and facility data collection, refinement, and OT security; form consortia with local governments, regional universities, and anchor companies to propose a PoC (Proof of Concept) to diffusion roadmap and quantitative KPIs (defect rate, OEE, kWh/unit, on-time delivery rate, downtime); and transition from outsourced PoCs to in-house personnel, MLOps, and integrated OT/IT governance, thereby responding to the trend of 'internalizing core technologies'.

Three government ministries and the Presidential Committee for Future Strategy will form a â€˜one teamâ€™ to accelerate AI transformation across all industries and operate a dedicated TF for manufacturing and industrial AX. The core elements are field-customized AX development focused on small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and mid-sized companies, internalization of core technologies, and creation of an ecosystem based on regional key industries. Manufacturing companies can secure an advantage in future public tenders and support projects by securing data and security readiness, establishing an internalization roadmap (MLOps, OT/IT integration), proposing PoC (Proof of Concept) and its expansion through regional consortia, and aligning with national project KPIs such as safety, quality, and energy saving.

As physiological adaptation has limits in responding to extreme temperatures, systematic management is key, which involves constantly monitoring heat and humidity indicators like WBGT through factory microclimate sensing and automatically triggering cooling, shade, hydration, and work intensity adjustments via an early warning system that combines weather forecasts, on-site sensors, and HR/EHS data. Taking individual differences into account, wearable data (such as heart rate, skin temperature, and perspiration) can be interpreted with AI to personalize work-rest cycles and PPE, and by utilizing physiological simulations/digital twins to pre-validate facility layout, ventilation, shifts, and work assignments, safety and utilization rates can be simultaneously optimized.

Research into human heat and cold responses suggests strategies for ensuring safety and operational rates in manufacturing sites. Wet-bulb temperature and individual differences are key to heat risk, and it is effective to dynamically optimize work-rest cycles, job assignments, and ventilation/cooling operations by integrating physiological simulation and early warning systems into EHS. Short-term improvements are possible with wearable-based personalized protection and low-cost equipment such as fans, mists, shade, and cooling rooms, and data governance along with establishing a culture of education and reporting are key to implementation.

Big Tech's BECCS investment trends suggest the need for early consideration of decarbonization options in manufacturing industries with heat-intensive processes, such as pulp and paper, biofuel production, and waste incineration. Practically, establish an LCA-based MRV system and internal carbon accounting rules that can distinguish between 'avoided emissions vs actual removal,' and manage the sustainability of biomass feedstock through digital tracking, such as sensors and satellites. For implementation feasibility, simulate energy balance, capture efficiency, and OPEX using a process-integrated digital twin; review the permanence, verification, and refund clauses of credit offtake agreements with a standard checklist; and diversify your carbon removal portfolio to prepare for policy and market volatility.

The trend of Big Tech companies acquiring carbon removal credits by capturing and storing biomass-based emissions generated from sources like paper mills (BECCS) is expanding. However, there is significant debate about whether truly negative emissions are achieved throughout the entire process, including biomass harvesting, transportation, and processing. Manufacturers must enhance their LCA and MRV systems with data pipelines and AI analysis, and establish internal accounting standards that clearly distinguish between 'avoided emissions' and 'actual removal'. Manage the sustainability, traceability, permanence, and leakage risk of biomass raw materials through digital tracking and independent verification. When integrating BECCS, use digital twins to pre-verify process integration, energy impact, and economic viability. It is crucial for credit offtake agreements to include performance guarantees, verification protocols, and fallback clauses to control risks, and to design KPIs and procurement principles that do not incentivize increased waste.

The common denominator among top global smartphone OEMs is AI-assisted assembly/inspection (Samsung), advanced robotics/quality systems (Apple), selective in-house component manufacturing (Huawei), localized production tailored for emerging markets (Transsion/TECNO), and AI design-manufacturing simultaneity (Google), suggesting that smart factory advancement and production network design are key to competitiveness. Prioritized implementation tasks include establishing real-time feedback loops for edge AI-based in-line vision/RF/acoustic testing, automating foldable CTQ and life cycle testing, responding to SKU diversity with modular lines, and optimizing TCO and risk through CKD/SKD, local BOM, and inventory segmentation in India, Africa, etc. Additionally, shorten ramp-up through NPI digital twins, implement camera alignment/calibration automation cells, and concurrently pursue S&OP precision enhancement based on AI demand forecasting.

Summarizing the operational and technological focus points of leading smartphone manufacturers in 2025, we present directions from a manufacturing AX perspective. Manufacturing sites are transitioning from 'dashboard observation' to closed-loop execution of process and quality decision-making through autonomous data management and agentic AI, while data-centric operations and sustainability/security requirements are simultaneously being strengthened. To effectively implement this, combine IIoT data with process context (master data, routing, recipes, equipment status) and establish standard data models and governance. Then, under guardrails such as Zero Trust, least privilege, model governance, and HITL (Human-in-the-Loop), pilot high-frequency decision-making (with separated edge inference/cloud learning, and KPI-based automatic/manual switching) to quantify improvements in FPY (First Pass Yield), cycle time, MTTR (Mean Time To Repair), and energy intensity.

The core of the article is that Agentic AI and autonomous data management transform manufacturing operations from observation-centric to execution-centric. For on-site application, safety guardrails such as standardized data models and governance, edge-cloud division of labor, Zero Trust, and model governance are essential. As a solution to labor shortages, it is necessary to increase work efficiency with copilots and autonomous workflows, and concurrently provide role transition training. Initially, piloting in repetitive and high-frequency decision-making areas and establishing auto/manual transition guardrails based on KPIs to secure scalability is practically effective.

This suggests that China is expanding export controls to include rare earth production and processing equipment, and potentially broadening the scope of regulations to cover overseas processed products that contain Chinese rare earths. ë² ì´ì§€ë¶ì€ AI íˆ¬ì í™•ëŒ€ì™€ ë¹„ìš© ì••ë ¥ ì†ì— ê¸°ì—…ë“¤ì´ ì •ê·œ ì¸ë ¥ì„ ì¤„ì´ê³  ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•˜ë©°, ì œì¡°ì‚¬ëŠ” í•µì‹¬-ìœ ì—° ì§ë¬´ë¥¼ ë¶„ë¦¬í•´ ì»¨í‹´ì „íŠ¸Â·íŒŒíŠ¸íƒ€ì„ ì¸ë ¥í’€ê³¼ í¬ë¡œìŠ¤ íŠ¸ë ˆì´ë‹ì„ ë³‘í–‰í•´ ë…¸ë™ê³µê¸‰ ì œì•½ì„ ë³´ì™„í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë™ì‹œì— ê´€ì„¸Â·ë¬¼ê°€ ìƒìŠ¹ì„ ìƒì‡„í•˜ë ¤ë©´ ì›ì‚°ì§€Â·ê³µê¸‰ì„  ë‹¤ë³€í™”ì™€ LTAÂ·í—¤ì§€ë¡œ ì›ê°€ë¥¼ ê³ ì •í•˜ê³ , AI/ìë™í™”(ë¹„ì „ê²€ì‚¬, ìƒì‚°ê³„íš ìµœì í™” ë“±)ë¥¼ ROI ì§€í‘œ(OEEÂ·ë¶ˆëŸ‰ë¥ Â·ì¸ë ¥ëŒ€ì²´ìœ¨)ë¡œ ìš°ì„ ìˆœìœ„í™”í•´ ë¹ ë¥¸ íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿ì„ ì‹¤í–‰í•˜ì„¸ìš”. ìˆ˜ìš” ë‘”í™”ë¥¼ ë°˜ì˜í•œ ë³´ìˆ˜ì  ìˆ˜ìš”ê³„íšê³¼ ì§€ì—­ë³„ ê²½ê¸° ì˜¨ë„ì°¨ ê¸°ë°˜ì˜ ìƒì‚°Â·íŒë§¤ ì¬ë°°ì¹˜, ê¸ˆë¦¬ ì™„í™” êµ­ë©´ ëŒ€ë¹„ CAPEX ì‹¤í–‰ ì¤€ë¹„ê°€ AX ì„±ê³¼ë¥¼ ê·¹ëŒ€í™”í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. The Beige Book suggests that companies are reducing their regular workforce amidst expanded AI investment and cost pressures. Manufacturers should separate core and flexible roles, concurrently utilizing a contingent and part-time talent pool and cross-training to compensate for labor supply constraints. Simultaneously, to offset rising tariffs and inflation, diversify origins and supply chains, fix costs with LTA and hedging, and prioritize AI/automation (e.g., vision inspection, production plan optimization) using ROI metrics (OEE, defect rate, workforce replacement rate) and execute rapid pilots. Conservative demand planning reflecting demand slowdown, reallocation of production and sales based on regional economic disparities, and readiness for CAPEX execution in preparation for an interest rate easing phase will maximize AX performance.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ì—°ì¤€ ë² ì´ì§€ë¶ì€ ê³ ìš©ì´ ëŒ€ì²´ë¡œ ì•ˆì •ì ì´ì§€ë§Œ ê¸°ì—…ë“¤ì´ ìˆ˜ìš” ë‘”í™”Â·ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±Â·AI íˆ¬ì í™•ëŒ€ë¡œ ì¸ë ¥ ê°ì¶•ê³¼ ì„ì‹œ/íŒŒíŠ¸íƒ€ì„ ì „í™˜ì„ í™•ëŒ€í•œë‹¤ê³  ë°í™ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê´€ì„¸ë¡œ ìƒì‚°ì›ê°€ê°€ ìƒìŠ¹í•˜ê³ , ì´ë¯¼ ì •ì±… ë³€í™”ë¡œ ì œì¡° ì¸ë ¥ ê³µê¸‰ì´ ì œì•½ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. EV ì„¸ì•¡ê³µì œ ì¢…ë£Œë¡œ ë‹¨ê¸° ìˆ˜ìš” ë‹¹ê¹€ì´ ë°œìƒí•˜ë©°, ê¸ˆë¦¬ ì¸í•˜ ê¸°ëŒ€ê°€ ì»¤ì§€ê³  ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡°ì—… ê´€ì ì—ì„œëŠ” ì»¨í‹´ì „íŠ¸ ì¸ë ¥ ì „ëµ êµ¬ì¶•, ìë™í™”Â·AI í”„ë¡œì íŠ¸ì˜ ROI ì¬ì ê²€ê³¼ ë¹ ë¥¸ íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿, ê´€ì„¸ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ê³ ë ¤í•œ ê³µê¸‰ì„  ë‹¤ë³€í™”Â·ê°€ê²© ì „ê°€, ìˆ˜ìš” ë‘”í™” ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ì— ë§ì¶˜ ìƒì‚°Â·ì¬ê³  ì¡°ì •, ê¸ˆë¦¬ í•˜ë½ê¸°ì— ëŒ€ë¹„í•œ CAPEX íŒŒì´í”„ë¼ì¸ ì¤€ë¹„ê°€ ì‹¤ì§ˆì  ëŒ€ì‘ í¬ì¸íŠ¸ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. The Fed's Beige Book states that employment is largely stable, but companies are increasing workforce reductions and expanding the shift to temporary/part-time workers due to slowing demand, uncertainty, and expanding AI investments. Tariffs are increasing production costs, and changes in immigration policy are constraining the supply of manufacturing labor. The termination of EV tax credits is causing a short-term pull-forward of demand, and expectations for interest rate cuts are growing. From a manufacturing perspective, practical response points include: establishing a contingent workforce strategy; re-evaluating the ROI of automation and AI projects and rapid piloting; diversifying supply lines and passing on prices, considering tariff risks; adjusting production and inventory in line with demand slowdown scenarios; and preparing a CAPEX pipeline in anticipation of a period of falling interest rates.

DIATwin-based virtual commissioning pre-verifies equipment/line layouts and cycle times, reducing ramp-up time and initial quality risks, while DIASSA Smart Fastening implements closed-loop quality and traceability through the standardization of torque, angle, and time data and MES/QMS integration. Additionally, by integrating SCARA robots with vision and sensors, it lowers the variability of assembly/inspection processes, and proposes an implementation strategy that simultaneously achieves productivity and sustainability, such as improving energy efficiency by linking power monitoring with KPIs.

Delta Electronics introduced its digital twin-based virtual equipment development platform (DIATwin), smart screwdriving (DIASSA, electric screwdriver), and SCARA robots at ITAP 2025. This content is useful for understanding the direction of manufacturing digitalization, quality traceability, and high-speed assembly automation. From a practical perspective, key application areas include shortening run-up time through virtual commissioning, implementing closed-loop quality by linking fastening data with MES/QMS, standardizing SCARA + vision integration, and reviewing equipment energy monitoring systems. However, due to the lack of specific performance indicators or case studies, its value as reference material is moderate.
